	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">George Frideric Handel</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Handel" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Handel_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Handel (disambiguation)">Handel (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">18th-century German, later British, Baroque composer</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<table class="infobox biography vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><div class="fn" style="display:inline">George Frideric Handel</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Frideric_Handel_by_Balthasar_Denner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="George Frideric Handel by Balthasar Denner.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/George_Frideric_Handel_by_Balthasar_Denner.jpg/220px-George_Frideric_Handel_by_Balthasar_Denner.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="266" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/George_Frideric_Handel_by_Balthasar_Denner.jpg/330px-George_Frideric_Handel_by_Balthasar_Denner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/George_Frideric_Handel_by_Balthasar_Denner.jpg/440px-George_Frideric_Handel_by_Balthasar_Denner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2901" /></a><div>Portrait of Handel, <span class="nowrap">by <a href="/wiki/Balthasar_Denner" title="Balthasar Denner">Balthasar Denner</a></span> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201; 1726–1728</span>)</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Born</th><td><div style="display:inline" class="nickname">Georg Friederich Händel</div><br />23 February 1685 <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">(O.S.)</a><br /><div style="display:inline" class="birthplace"><a href="/wiki/Halle_(Saale)" title="Halle (Saale)">Halle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Magdeburg" title="Duchy of Magdeburg">Duchy of Magdeburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussia</a></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Died</th><td>14 April 1759 (aged 74)<br /><div style="display:inline" class="deathplace"><a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Burial place</th><td class="label"><a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Signature</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Frideric_Handel_Signature.svg" class="image"><img alt="George Frideric Handel Signature.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/George_Frideric_Handel_Signature.svg/150px-George_Frideric_Handel_Signature.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="33" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/George_Frideric_Handel_Signature.svg/225px-George_Frideric_Handel_Signature.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/George_Frideric_Handel_Signature.svg/300px-George_Frideric_Handel_Signature.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="257" data-file-height="56" /></a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>George Frideric</b> (or <b>Frederick</b>) <b>Handel</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/əl/: &#39;le&#39; in &#39;bottle&#39;">əl</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> born <span lang="de" style="font-style:normal;" title="German language text"><b>Georg Friederich Händel</b></span><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈɡeːɔʁk&#160;ˈfʁiːdʁɪç ˈhɛndl̩]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/De-Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Georg Friedrich Händel.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; 23 February 1685 <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">(O.S.)</a> [(N.S.) 5 March] – 14 April 1759)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHicks1998614_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHicks1998614-4">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> was a German, later British, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque</a> composer who spent the bulk of his career in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, becoming well known for his <a href="/wiki/Baroque_opera" class="mw-redirect" title="Baroque opera">operas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oratorio" title="Oratorio">oratorios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthem" title="Anthem">anthems</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Organ_concerto" title="Organ concerto">organ concertos</a>. Handel received important training in <a href="/wiki/Halle_(Saale)" title="Halle (Saale)">Halle</a> and worked as a composer in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> and Italy before settling in London in 1712; he <a href="/wiki/Handel%27s_Naturalisation_Act_1727" title="Handel&#39;s Naturalisation Act 1727">became a naturalised British subject in 1727</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He was strongly influenced both by the great composers of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Baroque" title="Italian Baroque">Italian Baroque</a> and by the middle-German <a href="/wiki/Polyphony" title="Polyphony">polyphonic</a> choral tradition.
</p><p>Within fifteen years, Handel had started three commercial opera companies to supply the English nobility with Italian opera. Musicologist <a href="/wiki/Winton_Dean" title="Winton Dean">Winton Dean</a> writes that his operas show that "Handel was not only a great composer; he was a dramatic genius of the first order."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDean196919_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDean196919-9">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> As <i><a href="/wiki/Alexander%27s_Feast_(Handel)" title="Alexander&#39;s Feast (Handel)">Alexander's Feast</a></i> (1736) was well received, Handel made a transition to English choral works. After his success with <i><a href="/wiki/Messiah_(Handel)" title="Messiah (Handel)">Messiah</a></i> (1742) he never composed an Italian opera again. Almost blind, and having lived in England for nearly fifty years, he died in 1759, a respected and rich man. His funeral was given full state honours, and he was buried in <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> in London.
</p><p>Born the same year as <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Scarlatti" title="Domenico Scarlatti">Domenico Scarlatti</a>, Handel is regarded as one of the greatest composers of the Baroque era, with works such as <i><a href="/wiki/Messiah_(Handel)" title="Messiah (Handel)">Messiah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Water_Music" title="Water Music">Water Music</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Music_for_the_Royal_Fireworks" title="Music for the Royal Fireworks">Music for the Royal Fireworks</a></i> remaining steadfastly popular.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuelow2004476_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuelow2004476-10">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> One of his four <a href="/wiki/Coronation_Anthems_(Handel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronation Anthems (Handel)">coronation anthems</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Zadok_the_Priest" title="Zadok the Priest">Zadok the Priest</a></i> (1727), composed for the coronation of <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II</a>, has been performed at every subsequent <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">British coronation</a>, traditionally during the sovereign's anointing. Another of his English oratorios, <i><a href="/wiki/Solomon_(Handel)" title="Solomon (Handel)">Solomon</a></i> (1748), has also remained popular, with the Sinfonia that opens act 3 (known more commonly as "The Arrival of the Queen of Sheba") featuring at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">2012 London Olympics opening ceremony</a>. Handel composed more than forty operas in over thirty years, and since the late 1960s, with the revival of baroque music and <a href="/wiki/Historically_informed_performance" title="Historically informed performance">historically informed musical performance</a>, interest in Handel's <a href="/wiki/Opera_seria" title="Opera seria">operas</a> has grown.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg/220px-George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg/330px-George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg/440px-George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1804" data-file-height="1238" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Frideric_Handel_baptismal_register.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Handel's baptismal registration (Marienbibliothek in <a href="/wiki/Halle_(Saale)" title="Halle (Saale)">Halle</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>Handel was born in 1685 in <a href="/wiki/Halle_(Saale)" title="Halle (Saale)">Halle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Magdeburg" title="Duchy of Magdeburg">Duchy of Magdeburg</a> (then part of <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussia</a>), to <a href="/wiki/Georg_H%C3%A4ndel" title="Georg Händel">Georg Händel</a> and Dorothea Taust.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> His father, aged sixty-three when George Frideric was born, was an eminent barber-surgeon who served the court of <a href="/wiki/Saxe-Weissenfels" title="Saxe-Weissenfels">Saxe-Weissenfels</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margraviate of Brandenburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144–6_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144–6-12">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Georg Händel was the son of a <a href="/wiki/Coppersmith" title="Coppersmith">coppersmith</a>, Valentin Händel (1582–1636), who had emigrated from <a href="/wiki/Eisleben" title="Eisleben">Eisleben</a> in 1608 with his first wife Anna Belching, the daughter of a master coppersmith. They were Protestants and chose reliably Protestant Saxony over <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg</a> possession, as religious tensions mounted in the years before the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Thirty Years War">Thirty Years War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Halle was a relatively prosperous city, home of a salt-mining industry and center of trade (and member of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Margrave of Brandenburg became the administrator of the archiepiscopal territories of <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Magdeburg" title="Archbishopric of Magdeburg">Magdeburg</a> when they converted, and by the early 17th century held his court in Halle, which attracted renowned musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> Even the smaller churches all had "able organists and fair choirs",<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> and humanities and the letters thrived (Shakespeare was performed in the theaters early in the 17th century).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196620_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196620-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Thirty Years War brought extensive destruction to Halle, and by the 1680s it was impoverished.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> However, since the middle of the war the city had been under the administration of the <a href="/wiki/Augustus,_Duke_of_Saxe-Weissenfels" title="Augustus, Duke of Saxe-Weissenfels">Duke of Saxony</a>, and soon after the end of the war he would bring musicians trained in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a> to his court in <a href="/wiki/Wei%C3%9Fenfels" title="Weißenfels">Weissenfels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrows19941–2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrows19941–2-19">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg/220px-Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg/330px-Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg/440px-Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3676" data-file-height="2788" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Halle_H%C3%A4ndelhaus_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/w/index.php?title=H%C3%A4ndel-Haus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Händel-Haus (page does not exist)">Händel-Haus</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/H%C3%A4ndel-Haus" class="extiw" title="de:Händel-Haus">de</a>&#93;</span>, birthplace of Handel</div></div></div>
<p>The arts and music, however, flourished only among the higher strata (not only in Halle but throughout Germany),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196625–26_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196625–26-20">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> of which Handel's family was not a member. Georg Händel (senior) was born at the beginning of the war, and was apprenticed to a barber in Halle at the age of 14, after his father died.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup> When he was 20, he married the widow of the official barber-surgeon of a suburb of Halle, inheriting his practice. With this, Georg determinedly began the process of becoming self-made; by dint of his "conservative, steady, thrifty, unadventurous" lifestyle,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196610_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196610-22">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> he guided the five children he had with Anna who reached adulthood into the medical profession (except his youngest daughter, who married a government official).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144–45_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdamsHofestädt2005144–45-23">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Anna died in 1682. Within a year Georg married again, this time to the daughter of a Lutheran minister, Pastor Georg Taust of the Church of St. Bartholomew in Giebichtenstein,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELandon19849_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELandon19849-24">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> who himself came from a long line of Lutheran pastors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196610_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196610-22">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Handel was the second child of this marriage; the first son was <a href="/wiki/Stillbirth" title="Stillbirth">stillborn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutsch19556_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutsch19556-25">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Two younger sisters were born after the birth of George Frideric: Dorthea Sophia, born 6 October 1687, and Johanna Christiana, born 10 January 1690.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_education">Early education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG/220px-HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG/330px-HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG/440px-HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1436" data-file-height="785" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HALL_IN_SAXEN_-_Der_getreue_Rei%C3%9F-Gefert..._-_1686.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Halle, copper engraving, 1686</div></div></div>
<p>Early in his life Handel is reported to have attended the <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasium</a> in Halle,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDreyhaupt1755625_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDreyhaupt1755625-27">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> where the headmaster, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johann_Praetorius_(musician)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Johann Praetorius (musician) (page does not exist)">Johann Praetorius</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Praetorius_(Musiker)" class="extiw" title="de:Johann Praetorius (Musiker)">de</a>&#93;</span>, was reputed to be an ardent musician.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaitlandSquire1890277_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaitlandSquire1890277-28">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Whether Handel remained there or for how long is unknown, but many biographers suggest that he was withdrawn from school by his father, based on the characterization of him by Handel's first biographer, <a href="/wiki/John_Mainwaring" title="John Mainwaring">John Mainwaring</a>. Mainwaring is the source for almost all information (little as it is) of Handel's childhood, and much of that information came from J.C. Smith, Jr., Handel's confidant and copyist.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Whether it came from Smith or elsewhere, Mainwaring frequently relates misinformation.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> It is from Mainwaring that the portrait comes of Handel's father as implacably opposed to any musical education. Mainwaring writes that Georg Händel was "alarmed" at Handel's very early propensity for music,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> "took every measure to oppose it", including forbidding any musical instrument in the house and preventing Handel from going to any house where they might be found.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring17604–5_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring17604–5-33">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This did nothing to dampen young Handel's inclination; in fact, it did the reverse. Mainwaring tells the story of Handel's secret attic <a href="/wiki/Spinet" title="Spinet">spinet</a>: Handel "found means to get a little <a href="/wiki/Clavichord" title="Clavichord">clavichord</a> privately convey'd to a room at the top of the house. To this room he constantly stole when the family was asleep".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring17605_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring17605-34">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Although both <a href="/wiki/John_Hawkins_(author)" title="John Hawkins (author)">John Hawkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Burney" title="Charles Burney">Charles Burney</a> credited this tale, Schoelcher found it nearly "incredible" and a feat of "poetic imagination"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18574_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18574-35">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and Lang considers it one of the unproven "romantic stories" that surrounded Handel's childhood.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196611_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196611-36">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> But Handel had to have had some experience with the keyboard to have made the impression in Weissenfels that resulted in his receiving formal musical training.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDent20043–4_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDent20043–4-37">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_education">Musical education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Musical education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sometime between the ages of seven and nine, Handel accompanied his father to <a href="/wiki/Weissenfels" class="mw-redirect" title="Weissenfels">Weissenfels</a> where he came under the notice of one whom Handel thereafter always regarded throughout life as his benefactor,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18575_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18575-38">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johann_Adolf_I,_Duke_of_Saxe-Weissenfels" title="Johann Adolf I, Duke of Saxe-Weissenfels">Duke Johann Adolf I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup> Somehow Handel made his way to the court organ in the palace chapel of the Holy Trinity, where he surprised everyone with his playing.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Overhearing this performance and noting the youth of the performer caused the Duke, whose suggestions were not to be disregarded, to recommend to Georg Händel that Handel be given musical instruction.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Handel's father engaged the organist at the Halle parish church, the young <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Wilhelm_Zachow" title="Friedrich Wilhelm Zachow">Friedrich Wilhelm Zachow</a>, to instruct Handel. Zachow would be the only teacher that Handel ever had.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196611_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196611-36">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Because of his church employment, Zachow was an organist "of the old school", reveling in fugues, canons and counterpoint.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18575_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18575-38">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> But he was also familiar with developments in music across Europe and his own compositions "embraced the new concerted, dramatic style".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;j&#93;</a></sup> When Zachow discovered the talent of Handel, he introduced him "to a vast collection of German and Italian music, which he possessed, sacred and profane, vocal and instrumental compositions of different schools, different styles, and of every master".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18575_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18575-38">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Many traits considered "Handelian" can be traced back to Zachow's music.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> At the same time Handel continued practice on the <a href="/wiki/Harpsichord" title="Harpsichord">harpsichord</a>, learned <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organ_(music)" title="Organ (music)">organ</a>, but according to <a href="/wiki/Charles_Burney" title="Charles Burney">Burney</a> his special affection was for the <i>hautbois</i> (<a href="/wiki/Oboe" title="Oboe">oboe</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Schoelcher speculates that his youthful devotion to the instrument explains the large number of pieces he composed for oboe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18576_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18576-48">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg/220px-Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg/330px-Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg/440px-Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3883" data-file-height="3930" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marktkirche_halle_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marktkirche in Halle where Zachow and Handel performed as organists</div></div></div>
<p>With respect to instruction in composition, in addition to having Handel apply himself to traditional <a href="/wiki/Fugue" title="Fugue">fugue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cantus_firmus" title="Cantus firmus">cantus firmus</a> work, Zachow, recognizing Handel's precocious talents, systematically introduced Handel to the variety of styles and masterworks contained in his extensive library. He did this by requiring Handel to copy selected scores. "I used to write like the devil in those days", Handel recalled much later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196612_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196612-49">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Much of this copying was entered into a notebook that Handel maintained for the rest of his life. Although it has since disappeared, the notebook has been sufficiently described to understand what pieces Zachow wished Handel to study. Among the chief composers represented in this exercise book were <a href="/wiki/Johann_Krieger" title="Johann Krieger">Johann Krieger</a>, an "old master" in the fugue and prominent organ composer, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Caspar_Kerll" title="Johann Caspar Kerll">Johann Caspar Kerll</a>, a representative of the "southern style" after his teacher <a href="/wiki/Frescobaldi" title="Frescobaldi">Frescobaldi</a> and imitated later by Handel,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;k&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johann_Jakob_Froberger" title="Johann Jakob Froberger">Johann Jakob Froberger</a>, an "internationalist" also closely studied by <a href="/wiki/Dieterich_Buxtehude" title="Dieterich Buxtehude">Buxtehude</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georg_Muffat" title="Georg Muffat">Georg Muffat</a>, whose amalgam of French and Italian styles and his synthesis of musical forms influenced Handel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196613–16_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196613–16-52">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mainwaring writes that during this time Zachow had begun to have Handel assume some of his church duties. Zachow, Mainwaring asserts, was "often" absent, "from his love of company, and a chearful glass", and Handel therefore performed on organ frequently.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176015_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176015-53">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> What is more, according to Mainwaring, Handel began composing, at the age of nine, church services for voice and instruments "and from that time actually did compose a service every week for three years successively."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176016_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176016-54">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Mainwaring ends this chapter of Handel's life by concluding that three or four years had been enough to allow Handel to surpass Zachow, and Handel had become "impatient for another situation"; "Berlin was the place agreed upon."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176018_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176018-55">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Carelessness with dates or sequences (and possibly imaginative interpretation by Mainwaring) makes this period confused.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;l&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="After_the_death_of_Handel.27s_father"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_death_of_Handel's_father">After the death of Handel's father</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: After the death of Handel&#039;s father">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Handel's father died on 11 February 1697.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It was German custom for friends and family to compose funeral odes for a substantial burgher like Georg,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196619_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196619-58">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and young Handel discharged his duty with a poem dated 18 February and signed with his name and (in deference to his father's wishes) "dedicated to the liberal arts."<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> At the time Handel was studying either at Halle's Lutheran Gymnasium or the Latin School.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196619_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196619-58">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mainwaring has Handel traveling to Berlin the next year, 1698.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176018_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176018-55">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The problem with Mainwaring as an authority for this date, however, is that he tells of how Handel's father communicated with the "king"<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;m&#93;</a></sup> during Handel's stay, declining the Court's offer to send Handel to Italy on a stipend<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176024–25_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176024–25-62">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and that his father died "after his return from Berlin."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176029_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176029-63">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> But since Georg Händel died in 1697, either the date of the trip or Mainwaring's statements about Handel's father must be in error. Early biographers solved the problem by making the year of the trip 1696, then noting that at the age of 11 Handel would need a guardian, so they have Handel's father or a friend of the family accompany him, all the while puzzling over why the elder Handel, who wanted Handel to become a lawyer, would spend the sum to lead his son further into the temptation of music as a career.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang1966166_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang1966166-64">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Schoelcher for example has Handel traveling to Berlin at 11, meeting both <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bononcini" title="Giovanni Bononcini">Bononcini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Attilio_Ariosti" title="Attilio Ariosti">Attilio Ariosti</a> in Berlin and then returning at the direction of his father.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18576–7_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchoelcher18576–7-65">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> But Ariosti was not in Berlin before the death of Handel's father,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELandon198431_n.8_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELandon198431_n.8-66">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and Handel could not have met Bononcini in Berlin before 1702.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELandon198431_n.7_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELandon198431_n.7-67">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Modern biographers either accept the year as 1698, since most reliable older authorities agree with it,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;n&#93;</a></sup> and discount what Mainwaring says about what took place during the trip or assume that Mainwaring conflated two or more visits to Berlin, as he did with Handel's later trips to Venice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELandon198431_n.7_&amp;_53_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELandon198431_n.7_&amp;_53-69">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University">University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Perhaps to fulfill a promise to his father or simply because he saw himself as "dedicated to the liberal arts," on 10 February 1702 Handel matriculated at the <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_University_of_Halle-Wittenberg" title="Martin Luther University of Halle-Wittenberg">University of Halle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> That university had only recently been founded. In 1694 the <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick I of Prussia">Elector of Brandenburg Frederick III</a> (later Prussian King Frederick I) created the school, largely to provide a lecture forum for the jurist <a href="/wiki/Christian_Thomasius" title="Christian Thomasius">Christian Thomasius</a> who had been expelled from <a href="/wiki/Leipzig_University" title="Leipzig University">Leipzig</a> for his liberal views.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196620_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196620-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Händel did not enroll in the faculty of law, although he almost certainly attended lectures.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Thomasius was an intellectual and academic crusader who was the first German academic to lecture in German and also denounced witch trials. Lang believes that Thomasius instilled in Händel a "respect for the dignity and freedom of man's mind and the solemn majesty of the law," principles that would have drawn him to and kept him in England for half a century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196620–21_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196620–21-72">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Handel also there encountered theologian and professor of Oriental languages <a href="/wiki/August_Hermann_Francke" title="August Hermann Francke">August Hermann Francke</a>, who was particularly solicitous of children, particularly orphans. The orphanage he founded became a model for Germany, and undoubtedly influenced Handel's own charitable impulse, when he assigned the rights of <i>Messiah</i> to London's Foundling Hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196621_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196621-73">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dom_Halle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Dom_Halle.jpg/220px-Dom_Halle.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Dom_Halle.jpg/330px-Dom_Halle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Dom_Halle.jpg/440px-Dom_Halle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1017" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dom_Halle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Domkirche in Halle</div></div></div>
<p>Shortly after commencing his university education, Handel (though Lutheran<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;o&#93;</a></sup>) on 13 March 1702 accepted the position of organist at the Calvinist Cathedral in Halle, the Domkirche, replacing J.C. Leporin, for whom he had acted as assistant.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDent20042_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDent20042-76">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The position, which was a one-year probationary appointment showed the foundation he had received from Zachow, for a church organist and cantor was a highly prestigious office. From it he received 5 thalers a year and lodgings in the run-down castle of Moritzburg. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrows199420_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrows199420-77">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Around this same time Handel made the acquaintance of <a href="/wiki/Georg_Philipp_Telemann" title="Georg Philipp Telemann">Telemann</a>. Four years Handel's senior, Telemann was studying law and assisting cantor <a href="/wiki/Johann_Kuhnau" title="Johann Kuhnau">Johann Kuhnau</a> (<a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a>'s predecessor at the <a href="/wiki/Thomaskirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomaskirche">Thomaskirche</a> there). Telemann recalled forty years later in an autobiography for Mattheson's <i>Grundlage</i>: "The writing of the excellent Johann Kuhnau served as a model for me in fugue and counterpoint; but in fashioning melodic movements and examining them Handel and I were constantly occupied, frequently visiting each other as well as writing letters."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Halle_compositions">Halle compositions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Halle compositions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although Mainwaring records that Handel wrote weekly when assistant to Zachow and as probationary organist at Domkirche part of his duty was to provide suitable music,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;p&#93;</a></sup> no sacred compositions from his Halle period can now be identified.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196622_n.2_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196622_n.2-81">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Mattheson, however, summarized his opinion of Handel's church cantatas written in Halle: "Handel in those days set very, very long arias and sheerly unending cantatas which, while not possessing the proper knack or correct taste, were perfect so far as harmony is concerned."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Early chamber works do exist, but it is difficult to date any of them to Handel's time in Halle. Many historians until recently followed Chrysander and designated the six trio sonatas for two oboes and basso continuo as his first known composition, supposedly written in 1696 (when Handel was 11).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutsch19554_n.1_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutsch19554_n.1-83">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Lang doubts the dating based on a handwritten date of a copy (1700) and stylistic considerations. Lang writes that the works "show thorough acquaintance with the distilled sonata style of the <a href="/wiki/Arcangelo_Corelli" title="Arcangelo Corelli">Corelli school</a>" and are notable for "the formal security and the cleanness of the texture."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196623_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196623-84">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Hogwood considers all of the oboe trio sonatas spurious and even suggests that some parts cannot be performed on oboe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHogwood198421_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHogwood198421-85">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>  That authentic manuscript sources do not exist and that Handel never recycled any material from these works make their authenticity doubtful.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBest1985486–89_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBest1985486–89-86">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Other early chamber works were printed in Amsterdam in 1724 as opus 1, but it is impossible to tell which are early works in their original form, rather than later re-workings by Handel, a frequent practice of his.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196623_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196623-84">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="From_Halle_to_Italy">From Halle to Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: From Halle to Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburgs_Oper.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hamburgs_Oper.jpg/220px-Hamburgs_Oper.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hamburgs_Oper.jpg/330px-Hamburgs_Oper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/94/Hamburgs_Oper.jpg 2x" data-file-width="369" data-file-height="248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburgs_Oper.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_State_Opera" title="Hamburg State Opera">Hamburg Opera am Gänsemarkt</a> in 1726</div></div></div>
<p>Handel's probationary appointment to Domkirche expired in March 1703. By July<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;q&#93;</a></sup> Handel was in Hamburg. Since he left no explanation for the move<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;r&#93;</a></sup> biographers have offered their own speculation. Burrows believes that the answer can be found by untangling Mainwaring's confused chronology of the trip to Berlin. Burrows dates this trip to 1702 or 1703 (after his father's death) and concluded that since Handel (through a "friend and relation" at the Berlin court) turned down Frederick's offer to subsidize his musical education in Italy (with the implicit understanding that he would become a court musician on his return), Handel was no longer able to expect preferment (whether as musician, lawyer or otherwise) within Brandenburg-Prussia. And since he was attracted to secular, dramatic music (by meeting the Italians Bononcini and Attilio Ariosti and through the influence of Telemann), Hamburg, a free city with an established opera company, was the logical choice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrows199411–13_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrows199411–13-92">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The question remains, however, why Handel rejected the King's offer, given that Italy was the center of opera. Lang suggests that, influenced by the teachings of Thomasius, Handel's character was such that he was unable to make himself subservient to anyone, even a king. Lang sees Handel as someone who could not accept class distinctions that required him to regard himself as a social inferior. "What Handel craved was personal freedom to raise himself out of his provincial milieu to a life of culture."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang196626_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang196626-93">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Burrows notes that like his father, Handel was able to accept royal (and aristocratic) favors without considering himself a court servant.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrows199412_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrows199412-94">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> And so given the embarrassed financial condition of his mother,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176029_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176029-63">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Handel set off for Hamburg to obtain experience while supporting himself.
</p><p>In 1703 he accepted a position as violinist and harpsichordist in the orchestra of the Hamburg <a href="/wiki/Oper_am_G%C3%A4nsemarkt" title="Oper am Gänsemarkt">Oper am Gänsemarkt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> There he met the composers <a href="/wiki/Johann_Mattheson" title="Johann Mattheson">Johann Mattheson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Graupner" title="Christoph Graupner">Christoph Graupner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Keiser" title="Reinhard Keiser">Reinhard Keiser</a>. His first two operas, <i><a href="/wiki/Almira" title="Almira">Almira</a></i> and <i>Nero</i>, were produced in 1705.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> He produced two other operas, <i><a href="/wiki/George_Frideric_Handel%27s_lost_Hamburg_operas#Florindo_and_Daphne" class="mw-redirect" title="George Frideric Handel&#39;s lost Hamburg operas">Daphne</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Florindo" title="Florindo">Florindo</a></i>, in 1708. It is unclear whether Handel directed these performances.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG/170px-Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG/255px-Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG/340px-Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teatro_niccolini_11.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance of Teatro del Cocomero in Florence</div></div></div>
<p>According to Mainwaring, in 1706 Handel travelled to Italy at the invitation of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_(III)_de%27_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinando (III) de&#39; Medici">Ferdinando de' Medici</a>. Other sources say Handel was invited by <a href="/wiki/Gian_Gastone_de%27_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Gian Gastone de&#39; Medici">Gian Gastone de' Medici</a>, whom Handel had met in 1703–1704 in Hamburg.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris200137_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris200137-97">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> De' Medici, who had a keen interest in opera, was trying to make Florence Italy's musical capital by attracting the leading talents of his day. In Italy Handel met <a href="/wiki/Librettist" class="mw-redirect" title="Librettist">librettist</a> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Salvi" title="Antonio Salvi">Antonio Salvi</a>, with whom he later collaborated. Handel left for Rome and, since opera was (temporarily) banned in the <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a>, composed sacred music for the Roman clergy. His famous <i><a href="/wiki/Dixit_Dominus_(Handel)" title="Dixit Dominus (Handel)">Dixit Dominus</a></i> (1707) is from this era. He also composed <a href="/wiki/Cantata" title="Cantata">cantatas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pastoral" title="Pastoral">pastoral</a> style for musical gatherings in the palaces of duchess <a href="/wiki/Aurora_Sanseverino" title="Aurora Sanseverino">Aurora Sanseverino</a> (whom Mainwaring called "Donna Laura")<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> one of the most influential patrons from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Kingdom of Naples</a>, and cardinals <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Ottoboni_(cardinal)" title="Pietro Ottoboni (cardinal)">Pietro Ottoboni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benedetto_Pamphili" title="Benedetto Pamphili">Benedetto Pamphili</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colonna_family" title="Colonna family">Carlo Colonna</a>. Two <a href="/wiki/Oratorio" title="Oratorio">oratorios</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/La_resurrezione" title="La resurrezione">La resurrezione</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Il_trionfo_del_tempo_e_del_disinganno" class="mw-redirect" title="Il trionfo del tempo e del disinganno">Il trionfo del tempo</a></i>, were produced in a private setting for <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Maria_Marescotti_Ruspoli,_1st_Prince_of_Cerveteri" title="Francesco Maria Marescotti Ruspoli, 1st Prince of Cerveteri">Ruspoli</a> and Ottoboni in 1709 and 1710, respectively. <i><a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_(opera)" title="Rodrigo (opera)">Rodrigo</a></i>, his first all-Italian opera, was produced in the <a href="/wiki/Theatres_in_Florence" title="Theatres in Florence">Cocomero theatre</a> in Florence in 1707.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Agrippina_(opera)" title="Agrippina (opera)">Agrippina</a></i> was first produced in 1709 at <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Malibran" title="Teatro Malibran">Teatro San Giovanni Grisostomo</a>, owned by the <a href="/wiki/Grimani_family" title="Grimani family">Grimanis</a>. The opera, with a <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">libretto</a> by Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Grimani" title="Vincenzo Grimani">Vincenzo Grimani</a>, ran for 27 nights successively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176052_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMainwaring176052-100">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The audience, thunderstruck with the grandeur and sublimity of his style,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> applauded for <i>Il caro Sassone</i> ("the dear Saxon" – referring to Handel's German origins).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Move_to_London">Move to London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Move to London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg/220px-GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg/330px-GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg/440px-GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2594" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GeorgIvonGro%C3%9FbritannienGeorgFriedrichHaendelHamman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Handel <i>(centre)</i> and <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="George I of Great Britain and Ireland">King George I</a> on the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a>, 17 July 1717, by <a href="/wiki/Edouard_Hamman" title="Edouard Hamman">Edouard Hamman</a> (1819–88)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1710, Handel became <i><a href="/wiki/Kapellmeister" title="Kapellmeister">Kapellmeister</a></i> to German prince George, the <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Elector</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>, who in 1714 would become <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="George I of Great Britain and Ireland">King George I of Great Britain and Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> He visited <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Luisa_de%27_Medici" title="Anna Maria Luisa de&#39; Medici">Anna Maria Luisa de' Medici</a> and her husband in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> on his way to London in 1710. With his opera <i><a href="/wiki/Rinaldo_(opera)" title="Rinaldo (opera)">Rinaldo</a></i>, based on <i><a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Delivered" title="Jerusalem Delivered">La Gerusalemme Liberata</a></i> by the Italian poet <a href="/wiki/Torquato_Tasso" title="Torquato Tasso">Torquato Tasso</a>, Handel enjoyed great success, although it was composed quickly, with many borrowings from his older Italian works.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> This work contains one of Handel's favourite arias, <i>Cara sposa, amante cara</i>, and the famous <a href="/wiki/Lascia_ch%27io_pianga" title="Lascia ch&#39;io pianga">Lascia ch'io pianga</a>.
</p><p>In 1712, Handel decided to settle permanently in England. In the summer of 1713 he lived at Mr Mathew Andrews' estate in <a href="/wiki/Barn_Elms" title="Barn Elms">Barn Elms</a>, Surrey.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He received a yearly income of £200 from <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a> after composing for her the <i><a href="/wiki/Utrecht_Te_Deum_and_Jubilate" title="Utrecht Te Deum and Jubilate">Utrecht Te Deum and Jubilate</a></i>, first performed in 1713.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One of his most important patrons was <a href="/wiki/Richard_Boyle,_3rd_Earl_of_Burlington_and_4th_Earl_of_Cork" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Boyle, 3rd Earl of Burlington and 4th Earl of Cork">The 3rd Earl of Burlington and 4th Earl of Cork</a>, a young and extremely wealthy member of an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Irish">Anglo-Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy_(class)" title="Aristocracy (class)">aristocratic</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> While living in the mansion of Lord Burlington, Handel wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Amadigi_di_Gaula" title="Amadigi di Gaula">Amadigi di Gaula</a></i>, a "<a href="/wiki/Magician_(fantasy)" title="Magician (fantasy)">magic</a>" opera, about a <a href="/wiki/Damsel_in_distress" title="Damsel in distress">damsel in distress</a>, based on the tragedy by <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Houdar_de_la_Motte" title="Antoine Houdar de la Motte">Antoine Houdar de la Motte</a>.
</p><p>The conception of an opera as a coherent structure was slow to capture Handel's imagination<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and he composed no operas for five years. In July 1717 Handel's <i><a href="/wiki/Water_Music" title="Water Music">Water Music</a></i> was performed more than three times on the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a> for the King and his guests. It is said the compositions spurred reconciliation between Handel and the King, supposedly annoyed by the composer's abandonment of his Hanover post.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrows199477_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrows199477-110">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Cannons_.281717.E2.80.9319.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cannons_(1717–19)">Cannons (1717–19)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cannons (1717–19)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Handel_at_Cannons" title="Handel at Cannons">Handel at Cannons</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg/170px-Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg/255px-Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg/340px-Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="644" data-file-height="760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Georg_Friedrich_H%C3%A4ndel_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"The Chandos portrait of Georg Friedrich Händel"<br />by <a href="/wiki/James_Thornhill" title="James Thornhill">James Thornhill</a>, c. 1720</div></div></div>
<p>In 1717 Handel became house composer at <a href="/wiki/Cannons_(house)" title="Cannons (house)">Cannons</a> in <a href="/wiki/Middlesex" title="Middlesex">Middlesex</a>, where he laid the cornerstone for his future choral compositions in the <i><a href="/wiki/Chandos_Anthems" title="Chandos Anthems">Chandos Anthems</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBukofzer1947333–35_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBukofzer1947333–35-111">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Romain_Rolland" title="Romain Rolland">Romain Rolland</a> wrote that these anthems (or Psalms) stood in relation to Handel's oratorios, much the same way that the Italian cantatas stood to his operas: "splendid sketches of the more monumental works."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERolland191671_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERolland191671-112">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Another work, which he wrote for <a href="/wiki/James_Brydges,_1st_Duke_of_Chandos" title="James Brydges, 1st Duke of Chandos">The 1st Duke of Chandos</a>, the owner of Cannons, was <i><a href="/wiki/Acis_and_Galatea_(Handel)" title="Acis and Galatea (Handel)">Acis and Galatea</a></i>: during Handel's lifetime it was his most performed work. <a href="/wiki/Winton_Dean" title="Winton Dean">Winton Dean</a> wrote, "the music catches breath and disturbs the memory".<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1719 the Duke of Chandos became one of the composer's important patrons and main subscribers to his new opera company, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Music_(company)" title="Royal Academy of Music (company)">Royal Academy of Music</a>, but his patronage declined after Chandos lost money in the <a href="/wiki/South_Sea_Company" title="South Sea Company">South Sea bubble</a>, which burst in 1720 in one of history's greatest financial cataclysms. Handel himself invested in South Sea stock in 1716, when prices were low<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and sold before 1720.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Royal_Academy_of_Music_.281719.E2.80.9334.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Academy_of_Music_(1719–34)">Royal Academy of Music (1719–34)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Royal Academy of Music (1719–34)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Music_(company)" title="Royal Academy of Music (company)">Royal Academy of Music (company)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Handel_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/London_Handel_House.jpg/170px-London_Handel_House.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/London_Handel_House.jpg/255px-London_Handel_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/London_Handel_House.jpg/340px-London_Handel_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="993" data-file-height="1584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Handel_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Handel_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Handel House">Handel House</a> at 25 <a href="/wiki/Brook_Street" title="Brook Street">Brook Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayfair" title="Mayfair">Mayfair</a>, London</div></div></div>
<p>In May 1719, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pelham-Holles,_1st_Duke_of_Newcastle-upon-Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Pelham-Holles, 1st Duke of Newcastle-upon-Tyne">The 1st Duke of Newcastle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chamberlain" title="Lord Chamberlain">Lord Chamberlain</a>, ordered Handel to look for new singers.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Handel travelled to <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a> to attend the newly built opera. He saw <i>Teofane</i> by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Lotti" title="Antonio Lotti">Antonio Lotti</a>, and engaged members of the cast for the Royal Academy of Music, founded by a group of aristocrats to assure themselves a constant supply of baroque opera or <a href="/wiki/Opera_seria" title="Opera seria">opera seria</a>. Handel may have invited John Smith, his fellow student in Halle, and his son <a href="/wiki/John_Christopher_Smith" title="John Christopher Smith">Johann Christoph Schmidt</a>, to become his secretary and <a href="/wiki/Amanuensis" title="Amanuensis">amanuensis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> By 1723 he had moved into a <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> house at 25 <a href="/wiki/Brook_Street" title="Brook Street">Brook Street</a>, which he rented for the rest of his life.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> This house, where he rehearsed, copied music and sold tickets, is now the <a href="/wiki/Handel_House_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Handel House Museum">Handel House Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;s&#93;</a></sup> During twelve months between 1724 and 1725, Handel wrote three outstanding and successful operas, <i><a href="/wiki/Giulio_Cesare" title="Giulio Cesare">Giulio Cesare</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tamerlano" title="Tamerlano">Tamerlano</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rodelinda_(opera)" title="Rodelinda (opera)">Rodelinda</a></i>. Handel's operas are filled with <a href="/wiki/Da_capo_aria" title="Da capo aria">da capo arias</a>, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Svegliatevi_nel_core" title="Svegliatevi nel core">Svegliatevi nel core</a></i>. After composing <i>Silete venti</i>, he concentrated on opera and stopped writing cantatas. <i><a href="/wiki/Scipio_(opera)" class="mw-redirect" title="Scipio (opera)">Scipio</a></i>, from which the regimental slow march of the British <a href="/wiki/Grenadier_Guards" title="Grenadier Guards">Grenadier Guards</a> is derived,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> was performed as a stopgap, waiting for the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Faustina_Bordoni" title="Faustina Bordoni">Faustina Bordoni</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frederick,_Prince_of_Wales,_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Frederick%2C_Prince_of_Wales%2C_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg/220px-Frederick%2C_Prince_of_Wales%2C_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Frederick%2C_Prince_of_Wales%2C_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg/330px-Frederick%2C_Prince_of_Wales%2C_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Frederick%2C_Prince_of_Wales%2C_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg/440px-Frederick%2C_Prince_of_Wales%2C_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1858" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frederick,_Prince_of_Wales,_and_his_sisters_by_Philip_Mercier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A musical portrait of <a href="/wiki/Frederick,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Frederick, Prince of Wales">Frederick, Prince of Wales</a>, and his sisters by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Mercier" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip Mercier">Philip Mercier</a>, dated 1733, using <a href="/wiki/Kew_Palace" title="Kew Palace">Kew Palace</a> as its <i>plein-air</i> backdrop</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_(colour).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_%28colour%29.jpg/220px-Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_%28colour%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_%28colour%29.jpg/330px-Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_%28colour%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_%28colour%29.jpg/440px-Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_%28colour%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Italian_Opera_House_at_the_Haymarket_(colour).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Queen's Theatre in the <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haymarket (London)">Haymarket</a> in London by <a href="/wiki/William_Capon_(artist)" title="William Capon (artist)">William Capon</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1727 Handel was commissioned to write four anthems for the <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">Coronation</a> ceremony of <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">King George II</a>. One of these, <i><a href="/wiki/Zadok_the_Priest" title="Zadok the Priest">Zadok the Priest</a></i>, has been played at every British coronation ceremony since.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In 1728 John Gay's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beggar%27s_Opera" title="The Beggar&#39;s Opera">The Beggar's Opera</a></i>, which made fun of the type of Italian opera Handel had popularised in London, premiered at <a href="/wiki/Lisle%27s_Tennis_Court" title="Lisle&#39;s Tennis Court">Lincoln's Inn Fields Theatre</a> and ran for 62 consecutive performances, the longest run in theatre history up to that time.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> After nine years the Royal Academy of Music ceased to function but Handel soon started a new company.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Theatre" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Theatre">Queen's Theatre</a> at the Haymarket (now Her Majesty's Theatre), established in 1705 by architect and playwright <a href="/wiki/John_Vanbrugh" title="John Vanbrugh">John Vanbrugh</a>, quickly became an opera house.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Between 1711 and 1739, more than 25 of Handel's operas premièred there.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> In 1729 Handel became joint manager of the theatre with <a href="/wiki/John_James_Heidegger" title="John James Heidegger">John James Heidegger</a>.
</p><p>Handel travelled to Italy to engage new singers and also composed seven more operas, among them the comic masterpiece <i><a href="/wiki/Partenope" title="Partenope">Partenope</a></i> and the "magic" opera <i><a href="/wiki/Orlando_(opera)" title="Orlando (opera)">Orlando</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDent2004&#91;&#91;Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2019&#93;&#93;&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;&#91;&#91;Wikipedia:Citing_sources&#124;&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2019)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;&#93;&#93;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDent2004[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2019]]&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2019)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-125">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> After two commercially successful English oratorios <i><a href="/wiki/Esther_(Handel)" title="Esther (Handel)">Esther</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Deborah_(Handel)" title="Deborah (Handel)">Deborah</a></i>, he was able to invest again in the <a href="/wiki/South_Sea_Company" title="South Sea Company">South Sea Company</a>. Handel reworked his <i>Acis and Galatea</i> which then became his most successful work ever. Handel failed to compete with the <a href="/wiki/Opera_of_the_Nobility" title="Opera of the Nobility">Opera of the Nobility</a>, who engaged musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Johann_Adolph_Hasse" title="Johann Adolph Hasse">Johann Adolph Hasse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolo_Porpora" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolo Porpora">Nicolo Porpora</a> and the famous castrato <a href="/wiki/Farinelli" title="Farinelli">Farinelli</a>. The strong support by <a href="/wiki/Frederick,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Frederick, Prince of Wales">Frederick, Prince of Wales</a> caused conflicts in the royal family. In March 1734 Handel composed a wedding anthem <i><a href="/wiki/Wedding_anthem_for_Princess_Anne" title="Wedding anthem for Princess Anne">This is the day which the Lord hath made</a></i>, and a <a href="/wiki/Serenata" class="mw-redirect" title="Serenata">serenata</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Parnasso_in_Festa" class="mw-redirect" title="Parnasso in Festa">Parnasso in Festa</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal_and_Princess_of_Orange" title="Anne, Princess Royal and Princess of Orange">Anne, Princess Royal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Despite the problems the Opera of the Nobility was causing him at the time, Handel's neighbour in Brook Street, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Delany" title="Mary Delany">Mary Delany</a>, reported on a party she invited Handel to at her house on 12 April 1734 where he was in good spirits:</p><blockquote><p>I had Lady Rich and her daughter, Lady Cath. Hanmer and her husband, Mr. and Mrs. Percival, Sir John Stanley and my brother, Mrs. Donellan, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Strada" title="Anna Maria Strada">Strada</a> [star soprano of Handel's operas]  and Mr. Coot.  Lord Shaftesbury begged of Mr. Percival to bring him, and being a profess'd friend of Mr. Handel (who was here also) was admitted; I never was so well entertained at an opera!  Mr. Handel was in the best humour in the world, and played lessons and accompanied Strada and all the ladies that sang from seven o'clock till eleven.  I gave them tea and coffee, and about half an hour after nine had a salver brought in of chocolate, mulled white wine and biscuits.  Everybody was easy and seemed pleased.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span id="Opera_at_Covent_Garden_.281734.E2.80.9341.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Opera_at_Covent_Garden_(1734–41)">Opera at Covent Garden (1734–41)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Frideric_Handel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Opera at Covent Garden (1734–41)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg/220px-Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg/330px-Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg/440px-Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg 2x" data-file-width="837" data-file-height="617" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Covert_Garden_Theatre_edited.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Opera_House" title="Royal Opera House">Covent Garden Theatre</a> in London</div></div></div>
<p>In 1733 the <a href="/wiki/William_Capell,_3rd_Earl_of_Essex" title="William Capell, 3rd Earl of Essex">Earl of Essex</a> received a letter with the following sentence: "Handel became so arbitrary a prince, that the Town murmurs". The board of chief investors expected Handel to retire when his contract ended, but Handel immediately looked for another theatre. In cooperation with <a href="/wiki/John_Rich_(producer)" title="John Rich (producer)">John Rich</a> he started his third company at <a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Covent Garden Theatre">Covent Garden Theatre</a>. Rich was renowned for his spectacular productions. He suggested Handel use his small chorus and introduce the dancing of <a href="/wiki/Marie_Sall%C3%A9" title="Marie Sallé">Marie Sallé</a>, for whom Handel composed <i><a href="/wiki/Terpsicore" title="Terpsicore">Terpsicore</a></i>. In 1735 he introduced organ concertos between the acts. For the first time Handel allowed <a href="/wiki/Gioacchino_Conti" title="Gioacchino Conti">Gioacchino Conti</a>, who had no time to learn his part, to substitute arias.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Financially, <i><a href="/wiki/Ariodante" title="Ariodante">Ariodante</a></i> was a failure, although he introduced ballet suites at the end of each act.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Alcina" title="Alcina">Alcina</a></i>, his last opera with a magic content, and <i><a href="/wiki/Alexander%27s_Feast_(Handel)" title="Alexander&#39;s Feast (Handel)">Alexander's Feast</a> or the Power of Music</i> based on John Dryden's <i><a href="/wiki/Alexander%27s_Feast_(Dryden)" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander&#39;s Feast (Dryden)">Alexander's Feast</a></i> starred <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Strada_del_P%C3%B2" class="mw-redirect" title="Anna Maria Strada del Pò">Anna Maria Strada del Pò</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Beard_(tenor)" title="John Beard (tenor)">John Beard</a>.
</p><p>In April 1737, at age 52, Handel apparently suffered a stroke which disabled the use of four fingers on his right hand, preventing him from performing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurrows1994395_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurrows1994395-130">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In summer the disorder seemed at times to affect his understanding. Nobody expected that Handel would ever be able to perform again.
